Impulse input produces impulse response
741) Complex impedance form
Resistor: ZR = R
Capacitor: ZC = 1/(iωC)
Inductor: ZL = iωL
AC current: I = V/Z
Phase angle comes from the argument of Z
742) Resonance width and Q
Q = ω0/Δω for narrow resonance
Higher Q means sharper frequency selectivity
Energy stored decays more slowly when Q is larger
Linewidth is inversely related to lifetime
Applies to cavities, oscillators, and filters
743) Perturbation theory
H = H0 + H'
E = E0 + E(1) + E(2) + ...
E(1) = for nondegenerate states
Useful when H' is small compared with H0
Higher orders account for mixing between states
744) Degenerate perturbation
Diagonalize H' within degenerate subspace
Energy splitting comes from perturbation matrix eigenvalues
Correct states are linear combinations of original degenerate states
Needed whenever unperturbed levels share the same energy
Important in symmetry-related systems
745) Variational principle
E0 ≤ <ψ|H|ψ>/<ψ|ψ>
Trial wavefunctions give upper bounds to ground-state energy
Improving trial form lowers the estimate
Extremely useful when exact solutions are unavailable
Common in atomic, molecular, and solid-state physics
746) Time-independent Schrödinger equation
Hψ = Eψ
Stationary states have time dependence e^(-iEt/ħ)
Energy eigenvalues determine measurable energies
Boundary conditions quantize allowed states
Fundamental equation of nonrelativistic quantum mechanics
747) Probability current and continuity
ρ = |ψ|²
j = (ħ/2mi)(ψ∇ψ - ψ∇ψ)
∂ρ/∂t + ∇·j = 0
Total probability is conserved in closed systems
Useful for tunneling and scattering analysis
748) Matrix mechanics
Observable quantities are Hermitian operators
Eigenvalues correspond to measurement outcomes
Commutator [A, B] measures noncommutativity
Trace and determinant help classify operators
Unitary evolution preserves inner products
749) Pauli matrices
σx, σy, σz represent spin-1/2 operators
σiσj = δijI + iεijkσk
S = (ħ/2)σ
Two-level systems are often written in this basis
Useful for qubits and magnetic resonance
750) Spin precession
dS/dt = γ S × B
Spin precesses around magnetic field direction
Larmor frequency: ωL = γB
Observed in NMR and ESR
Precession rate depends on field magnitude
751) Selection rules
Rules constrain which transitions are allowed
For electric dipole: Δl = ±1
Often Δm = 0, ±1 depending on polarization
Parity change is required in many dipole transitions
Helps predict spectra and line intensities
752) Hydrogen-like atom scaling
En = -13.6 Z²/n² eV for hydrogen-like ions
Radius rn ∝ n²/Z
Transition energy scales strongly with Z
Bohr model gives rough trends
Higher nuclear charge compresses the atom
753) Fine-structure reminder
Relativistic correction shifts levels slightly
Spin-orbit coupling splits degenerate terms
Darwin term affects s-states
Corrections scale strongly with atomic number
Observed in precise atomic spectra
754) Zeeman effect reminder
Magnetic field splits atomic energy levels
ΔE ∝ mB B in simple cases
Normal Zeeman effect neglects spin complications
Anomalous Zeeman effect includes spin and total angular momentum
Used in magnetometry and spectroscopy
755) Stark effect reminder
Electric field shifts atomic or molecular levels
Linear Stark effect can occur in degenerate states
Quadratic Stark shift often dominates nondegenerate states
Polarizability controls the size of the shift
Important in field spectroscopy
756) Molecular rotation
EJ = BJ(J + 1)
B = ħ²/(2I)
ΔJ = ±1 for rotational transitions
Level spacing depends on moment of inertia
Microwave spectra probe rotational structure
757) Molecular vibration
En = (n + 1/2)ħω
Harmonic approximation near equilibrium bond length
IR activity requires a changing dipole moment
Reduced mass affects vibrational frequency
Anharmonicity shifts higher levels
758) Raman shift
Scattered photon frequency changes by vibrational energy difference
Stokes line has lower frequency than incident light
Anti-Stokes line has higher frequency than incident light
Intensity depends on polarizability change
Useful for molecular identification
759) Spectral linewidth
ΔEΔt ≥ ħ/2
Short lifetime broadens spectral line
Natural linewidth from finite excited-state lifetime
Doppler and collisional broadening can add further width
Observed line shape reflects multiple mechanisms
760) Planck radiation law
u(ν, T) = (8πhν³/c³)/(e^(hν/kBT) - 1)
Blackbody spectrum depends only on temperature
High-frequency tail is exponentially suppressed
Solves the ultraviolet catastrophe
Key result in quantum theory
761) Wien displacement
λmax T = b
Hotter objects peak at shorter wavelength
Useful for stars and thermal emitters
Direct consequence of blackbody spectrum
Explains color shift with temperature
762) Stefan-Boltzmann relation
P = εσAT⁴
Blackbody corresponds to ε = 1
Net radiative power depends strongly on temperature
Surface emissivity alters real-world power
Used in thermal engineering and astrophysics
763) Radiative heat balance
Net loss often modeled as εσA(T⁴ - Tenv⁴)
Radiation dominates at high temperature
Conduction and convection may be added separately
Useful for furnaces, spacecraft, and hot surfaces
Nonlinear temperature dependence is important
764) Heat capacity models
At constant volume: Cv = (∂U/∂T)V
At constant pressure: Cp = (∂H/∂T)P
Cp - Cv = R for ideal monatomic gas per mole
Quantum solids deviate from classical equipartition at low T
Heat capacity reveals microscopic degrees of freedom
765) Thermodynamic potentials
U = internal energy
H = U + PV
F = U - TS
G = H - TS
Each potential is natural for different constraints
Choice depends on fixed variables
766) Gibbs free energy
G = H - TS
At fixed T and P, spontaneous change lowers G
Equilibrium corresponds to minimum G
Useful in chemistry and phase transitions
Determines reaction direction and stability
767) Chemical equilibrium
At equilibrium, forward and reverse rates balance
Equilibrium constant related to free energy change
ΔG = ΔG° + RT ln Q
ΔG = 0 when Q = K
Key relation in physical chemistry
768) Electrochemical cell
ΔG = -nFEcell
Positive cell voltage corresponds to spontaneous reaction in standard sign convention
Nernst equation: E = E° - (RT/nF)ln Q
Concentration changes alter cell potential
Used in batteries and corrosion analysis
769) Diffusion equation
∂c/∂t = D∇²c
Concentration spreads from high to low values
D is the diffusion coefficient
Steady state with no sources gives ∇²c = 0
Used in heat, mass, and charge transport
770) Fick’s law
J = -D∇c
Flux points down concentration gradient
Combines with continuity to produce diffusion equation
Applicable to particles, molecules, and carriers
Foundation of transport modeling
771) Drift-diffusion current
Jn = qnμnE + qDn∇n
Jp = qpμpE - qDp∇p
Drift comes from electric field
Diffusion comes from concentration gradient
Core semiconductor transport relation
772) Hall effect
VH = IB/(nqt)
Hall coefficient RH = 1/(nq)
Sign of RH identifies carrier sign in simple models
Magnetic field deflects charge carriers sideways
Useful for carrier density measurements
773) Semiconductor diode
I = Is(e^(qV/nkBT) - 1)
Forward bias yields large current
Reverse bias gives approximately saturation current in ideal model
Depletion region controls transport
Base model for p-n junction behavior
774) MOS capacitor
Gate voltage controls surface charge through oxide dielectric
Accumulation, depletion, and inversion are distinct regimes
Threshold voltage marks onset of inversion channel
Important in MOSFET operation
Capacitance changes with bias
775) MOSFET current
Linear region and saturation region have different current laws
Channel charge is modulated by gate overdrive
Threshold voltage sets conduction onset
Essential for digital switching and analog amplification
Core component of integrated circuits
776) Transistor gain
Common-emitter current gain β = Ic/Ib
Transconductance gm = dIc/dVbe
Small-signal models linearize around bias point
Used to analyze amplifiers and switches
Gain depends on operating conditions
777) Superconducting relations
Zero resistance below critical temperature in ideal model
Meissner effect expels magnetic field from bulk
Critical field and critical current limit operation
Type-I and type-II behavior differ by field response
Quantum coherence is central
778) Josephson relations
I = Ic sin φ
dφ/dt = 2eV/ħ
AC Josephson frequency: f = 2eV/h
Supercurrent depends on phase difference
Basis of superconducting quantum circuits
779) Quantum tunneling
Wavefunction penetrates classically forbidden regions
Transmission probability decreases exponentially with barrier width and height
Important in alpha decay and tunnel junctions
Cannot be explained by classical mechanics
Key quantum effect in many devices
780) End-of-continuation note
Continue the sequence from this point without repeating earlier rows
Use the same one-column copy-md table structure for further expansion
Advanced topics can keep branching into specialized subfields
Rows: 280
Table 3
Physics Formula Bank Continued 7
781) Small-oscillation matrix form
M q¨ + K q = 0
Normal modes satisfy det(K - ω²M) = 0
Eigenvectors give mode shapes
Mass and stiffness matrices may be non-diagonal
Useful for coupled mechanical systems
782) Generalized coordinates
q = {q1, q2, ... , qn}
Constraints reduce degrees of freedom
Velocity follows from chain rule: ṙ = Σ(∂r/∂qi) q̇i
Coordinates need not be Cartesian
Convenient for systems with holonomic constraints
783) D’Alembert principle
Σ(Fi - mi ai)·δri = 0
Transforms dynamics into virtual-work form
Useful for constrained motion
Leads naturally to Lagrange equations
Helps eliminate unknown constraint forces
784) Virtual work
δW = Σ Fi·δri
For equilibrium, δW = 0 for allowed virtual displacements
Constraint forces often do no virtual work
Powerful statics and dynamics tool
Works best with ideal constraints
785) Routhian idea
R = Σ pi q̇i - L for cyclic variables eliminated
Combines features of Lagrangian and Hamiltonian methods
Useful when some coordinates are ignorable
Reduces dimensionality of a problem
Applies to partially constrained systems
786) Jacobi integral
EJ = T + Ueff in rotating-frame problems
Constant of motion in certain conservative rotating systems
Used in celestial mechanics and restricted three-body problems
Helps analyze stability regions
Arises from symmetry in rotating coordinates
787) Three-body effective potential
Ueff includes gravity and centrifugal terms
Lagrange points occur where ∇Ueff = 0
Equilibrium points can be stable or unstable
Useful in space mission design
Applied to restricted three-body motion
788) Lagrange points
Five equilibrium points exist in the circular restricted three-body problem
L1, L2, L3 lie on the line of centers
L4 and L5 form equilateral triangles
Stability depends on mass ratio
Used for spacecraft and orbital dynamics
789) Keplerian orbital elements
a = semi-major axis
e = eccentricity
i = inclination
Ω = longitude of ascending node
ω = argument of periapsis
ν = true anomaly
790) Vis-viva equation
v² = μ(2/r - 1/a)
μ = GM for central gravitating body
Gives orbital speed at any point on ellipse
Specializes to circular orbit when a = r
Central in astrodynamics
791) Specific angular momentum
h = r × v
|h| is conserved in central force motion
h determines orbital plane and geometry
For planar motion, h = rv⊥
Useful in orbit propagation
792) Orbital energy
ε = v²/2 - μ/r
For bound Kepler orbit, ε = -μ/(2a)
Negative energy indicates bound orbit
Escape trajectory has ε ≥ 0
Used to classify orbital states
793) Eccentricity vector
e = (v × h)/μ - r̂
Points toward periapsis
Magnitude equals orbital eccentricity
Constant in ideal inverse-square motion
Gives orbit shape directly
794) Kepler equation
M = E - e sin E
Relates mean anomaly to eccentric anomaly
Must usually be solved numerically
Connects time to orbital position
Core formula for elliptical orbits
795) Areal velocity
dA/dt = h/2
Constant by angular momentum conservation
Kepler’s second law expressed mathematically
Equal areas in equal times
Useful for estimating orbital timing
796) Rocket staging
Δvtotal = Σ ve ln(mi/mf)
Staging improves effective velocity budget
Mass ratio is critical for mission design
Exhaust velocity and payload dominate performance
Central in launch vehicle analysis
797) Tsiolkovsky with gravity loss
Δvusable = ve ln(m0/mf) - ∫g dt - drag losses
Real mission performance is less than ideal equation
Launch trajectory affects required propellant
Gravity turn reduces losses
Useful in practical ascent planning
798) Harmonic oscillator phase space
x²/A² + (v/ωA)² = 1 in ideal SHM
Phase-space trajectory is an ellipse
Area relates to action variable
Energy determines ellipse size
Useful for visualizing oscillatory motion
799) Damped oscillator energy decay
E(t) ∝ e^(-2βt)
Amplitude decays as e^(-βt)
Energy falls faster than amplitude
Damping constant sets decay rate
Used in resonator analysis
800) Forced oscillator response
A(ω) = F0/m / √((ω0² - ω²)² + (2βω)²)
Peak amplitude depends on damping and forcing frequency
Phase shift changes across resonance
Common in driven mechanical and electrical systems
Predicts amplification behavior
801) Parametric oscillator
x¨ + [ω0² + ε cos(Ωt)]x = 0
Periodic parameter modulation can destabilize motion
Resonance tongues appear in parameter space
Used in Mathieu-type systems
Important in optics and mechanics
802) Coupled pendulums
Normal mode frequencies split into symmetric and antisymmetric branches
Energy exchanges periodically between pendula
Coupling constant determines beat rate
Good model for mode hybridization
Analogous to many coupled oscillators
803) Pendulum with large amplitude
T = 4√(L/g) K(k)
K(k) is complete elliptic integral of the first kind
Exact period depends on amplitude
Small-angle formula is only approximation
Relevant for precision pendulum analysis
804) Elliptic integral of motion
Some nonlinear oscillators require elliptic functions for exact solution
Energy conservation yields integral form
Closed-form sinusoidal motion no longer sufficient
Common in finite-amplitude pendula and rigid-body motion
Useful in advanced mechanics
805) Rigid body Euler equations
I1 ω̇1 + (I3 - I2)ω2ω3 = τ1
I2 ω̇2 + (I1 - I3)ω3ω1 = τ2
I3 ω̇3 + (I2 - I1)ω1ω2 = τ3
Describe rotation in body-fixed frame
Important for spinning tops and spacecraft attitude
806) Torque-free precession
τ = 0 but rotation axis may still move in body frame
Angular momentum remains fixed in space frame
Energy and angular momentum constrain motion
Intermediate-axis instability can appear
Useful in rigid-body dynamics
807) Inertia ellipsoid
Rotational kinetic energy depends on axis direction
Moment of inertia varies with orientation
Principal axes diagonalize inertia tensor
Geometry controls rotational response
Used in robotics and spacecraft design
808) Coriolis acceleration
aC = -2Ω × vrel
Appears in rotating frames
Deflects moving objects to the side
Important in atmospheric and oceanic flows
Causes apparent force on rotating Earth
809) Foucault pendulum precession
Ωp = ΩEarth sin φ
Precession rate depends on latitude φ
Shows Earth’s rotation directly
Long-period motion is a Coriolis effect
Classic demonstration experiment
810) Geopotential height
Φ = ∫ g dz
Used in atmospheric science and geodesy
Potential height differs from geometric height when g varies
Helpful for pressure surfaces
Connects gravity and atmosphere
811) Hydrostatic atmosphere
dP/dz = -ρg
Combining with ideal gas law gives exponential pressure profile in isothermal case
Scale height H = kBT/(mg) in simple model
Explains pressure drop with altitude
Used in meteorology and planetary atmospheres
812) Adiabatic lapse rate
Γd = g/cp
Temperature decreases with height in rising unsaturated air parcel
Important in weather stability
Derived from adiabatic expansion
Core atmospheric relation
813) Buoyancy stability
Stable if parcel density exceeds environment density after displacement
Brunt-Väisälä frequency relates restoring oscillation in stratified fluid
Controls atmospheric and oceanic stability
Important for convection analysis
Used in fluid stratification
814) Brunt-Väisälä frequency
N² = (g/θ)(dθ/dz) in simple atmospheric form
N² > 0 indicates stable stratification
N² < 0 indicates convective instability
Determines internal gravity wave frequency
Central in geophysical fluid dynamics
815) Internal gravity waves
Frequency depends on stratification and wave direction
Buoyancy acts as restoring force
Common in oceans and atmosphere
Distinct from ordinary surface gravity waves
Important in planetary fluid motion
816) Reynolds stress concept
Turbulent velocity fluctuations transport momentum
Average equations include extra stress-like terms
Closure problem appears in turbulence modeling
Important for weather and engineering flows
Requires statistical modeling
817) Eddy viscosity
Modeled turbulent momentum transport may be written with an effective viscosity
Not a true molecular viscosity
Useful empirical closure for turbulence
Depends on flow scale and geometry
Common in engineering models
818) Compressibility factor
Z = PV/(nRT)
Z = 1 for ideal gas
Deviation measures nonideality
Can depend on pressure and temperature
Important in real-gas thermodynamics
819) Virial equation
Z = 1 + B(T)/Vm + C(T)/Vm² + ...
Expands real-gas behavior in powers of density
Coefficients depend on intermolecular forces
Useful for moderately dense gases
Connects to molecular interactions
820) van der Waals critical constants
Derived from a and b parameters in the van der Waals model
Predicts qualitative critical behavior
Shows coexistence of gas and liquid phases
Useful for understanding real-fluid corrections
Historical importance in thermodynamics
821) Maxwell relations
Derived from equality of mixed second derivatives of thermodynamic potentials
Link measurable partial derivatives
Examples arise from U, H, F, and G
Very useful for thermodynamic manipulation
Allow conversion between hard-to-measure quantities
822) Gibbs-Duhem relation
Σ Ni dμi = -S dT + V dP
Constrains intensive variables in mixtures
Important for chemical thermodynamics
Useful when working with solutions and alloys
Relates composition and chemical potentials
823) Clausius inequality
∮ δQ/T ≤ 0
Equality holds for reversible cycles
Encodes second law
Shows irreversibility of real processes
Foundational thermodynamic statement
824) Exergy balance
Useful work potential decreases with irreversibility
Exergy destruction = T0 Sgen
Measures lost opportunity to do work
Common in engineering thermodynamics
Environment temperature T0 is reference
825) Carnot refrigeration bound
COPmax = Tc/(Th - Tc)
Upper limit for ideal refrigerator
Improves as temperature lift decreases
Set only by reservoir temperatures
Important benchmark in cooling systems
826) Heat exchanger effectiveness
εHX = actual heat transfer / maximum possible heat transfer
Used to compare exchanger performance
Depends on flow arrangement and capacity rates
Important in thermal system design
Higher effectiveness means better performance
827) Radiation view-factor reciprocity
Ai Fij = Aj Fji
Geometric coupling is symmetric in weighted form
Used in enclosure radiation calculations
Necessary for energy balance consistency
Important in thermal modeling
828) Fermi temperature
TF = EF/kB
Below TF, fermions are strongly degenerate
Classical statistics fail
Important in metals and ultracold gases
Characterizes quantum regime
829) Fermi-Dirac low-temperature expansion
Thermal effects are confined near Fermi level
Only states within ~kBT contribute significantly
Explains linear electronic heat capacity
Important in low-temperature solid-state physics
Useful in metal theory
830) Sommerfeld expansion
Approximates integrals weighted by Fermi-Dirac distribution at low temperature
Provides corrections around Fermi energy
Widely used in metal thermodynamics
Connects quantum statistics to observables
Powerful approximation technique
831) Debye cutoff frequency
ωD chosen so total phonon modes match 3N in a solid
Debye temperature θD = ħωD/kB
Model reproduces low-temperature heat capacity trend
Useful in lattice thermodynamics
Approximate but very effective
832) Elastic wave speed
Longitudinal speed in rod depends on Young’s modulus and density
Shear speed depends on shear modulus and density
Mechanical waves in solids have multiple polarizations
Important in seismology and materials
Stiffness raises wave speed
833) Seismic P- and S-wave speeds
vp = √((K + 4G/3)/ρ)
vs = √(G/ρ)
K is bulk modulus and G is shear modulus
Used to infer interior structure of Earth
Fundamental in geophysics
834) Fresnel coefficients
Reflection and transmission depend on polarization and incidence angle
Different for s and p polarizations
Determine intensity at interfaces
Important in optics and coatings
From boundary conditions on E and B
835) Brewster angle
tan θB = n2/n1
Reflected p-polarized light vanishes at Brewster angle in ideal case
Used in laser optics and polarizers
Depends on refractive indices
Good for polarization control
836) Malus cascade
I = I0 cos² θ1 cos² θ2 ...
Multiple analyzers multiply intensity reduction
Useful in polarization filters
Transmission depends on angle sequence
Common optics application
837) Jones vector rotation
Rotation matrices change polarization basis
Retarders introduce relative phase between components
Linear, circular, and elliptical polarization represented compactly
Useful for coherent polarization optics
Matrix approach is standard
838) Berry phase
γB = i∮ · dλ
Geometric phase acquired under adiabatic cyclic evolution
Depends on path in parameter space
Important in quantum and wave phenomena
Not purely dynamical
839) Aharonov-Bohm phase
Δφ = (q/ħ)∮ A·dl
Vector potential can affect phase even where B = 0 locally
Shows physical significance of potentials
Observed in interference experiments
Important in quantum theory
840) Gauge transformation
A → A + ∇χ
V → V - ∂χ/∂t
Physical fields E and B remain unchanged
Gauge freedom simplifies electromagnetic formulations
Foundation of modern field theory
841) Wavefunction normalization in 3D
∫ |ψ(r)|² d³r = 1
Probability density is |ψ|²
Normalization constant ensures total probability unity
Critical for bound-state wavefunctions
Standard quantum requirement
842) Hydrogen radial quantum numbers
Radial solutions depend on n and l
Number of radial nodes = n - l - 1
Angular part depends on l and m
State classification by quantum numbers
Useful for orbital structure
843) Orbital nodes
Angular nodes = l
Radial nodes = n - l - 1
Total nodes = n - 1
Node structure determines orbital shape
Common in atomic physics
844) Quantum harmonic oscillator ladder
En = (n + 1/2)ħω
x operator connects adjacent levels
Selection rules often Δn = ±1 for dipole transitions
Ground state is nonzero energy
Prototype quantum system
845) Particle in a finite well
Allowed energies come from transcendental boundary equations
Wavefunction penetrates outside well
Bound states finite in number depending on well depth
Quantization not as simple as infinite box
Important realistic quantum model
846) Tunneling through rectangular barrier
Transmission roughly decays as e^(-2κa)
κ = √(2m(V0 - E))/ħ for E < V0
Barrier width a strongly affects probability
Quantum effect with no classical analogue
Important for semiconductors and nuclear decay
847) WKB tunneling exponent
T ∼ exp[-2∫ κ(x) dx]
Semiclassical estimate for slowly varying barriers
Useful when exact solution is difficult
Applies in quantum mechanics and wave physics
Connects forbidden region to decay rate
848) Harmonic approximation
V(x) ≈ V(x0) + 1/2 V''(x0)(x - x0)²
Near stable equilibrium, motion is approximately sinusoidal
Frequency determined by curvature of potential
Core approximation in physics and chemistry
Explains small oscillations widely
849) Anharmonic correction
Potential may include cubic or quartic terms
Leads to frequency shifts and mode coupling
Important for real molecules and solids
Breaks exact sinusoidal behavior
Causes overtone structure in spectroscopy
850) Selection-rule broadening
Nonidealities relax strict transition rules
Vibrations, collisions, and fields can enable weak forbidden lines
Observed spectra may contain weak extra features
Real materials deviate from ideal symmetry
Important in spectroscopy interpretation
851) Density of states in 3D free-electron gas
g(E) ∝ √E
Explains metallic transport and heat capacity trends
States increase with energy in 3D
Central in electron-gas theory
Underlying tool in condensed matter
852) 2D density of states
For a simple free 2D electron gas, DOS is energy independent
Useful in semiconductor quantum wells and layered materials
Leads to distinctive transport properties
Important for heterostructures
Dimension changes density behavior
853) 1D density of states
g(E) often diverges near band edges in idealized models
Relevant to quantum wires and nanotubes
Strong dimensional effects on transport
Important in mesoscopic physics
Different from 2D and 3D behavior
854) Effective mass tensor
m*^-1 = (1/ħ²) ∂²E/∂k_i∂k_j
Anisotropic band curvature leads to tensor mass
Carrier motion depends on direction in crystal
Used in semiconductors and metals
Captures band-structure anisotropy
855) Bloch theorem
ψk(r) = uk(r)e^(ik·r)
uk(r) has lattice periodicity
Electron states in periodic potentials are Bloch states
Foundation of band theory
Critical in crystalline solids
856) Brillouin zone
Reciprocal-space primitive cell
Band structure is often analyzed within first Brillouin zone
Zone boundaries correspond to Bragg reflection conditions
Central in solid-state physics
Geometry of reciprocal lattice matters
857) Bragg reflection condition
2d sin θ = nλ
Scattering from lattice planes produces constructive interference
Basis of X-ray diffraction
Used to determine crystal structure
Angle and spacing encode spacing between planes
858) Reciprocal lattice vector
G·R = 2πm for lattice vector R
Describes periodicity in reciprocal space
Used in diffraction and band theory
Momentum transfer often involves reciprocal vectors
Foundation of crystallography
859) Phonon dispersion
ω = ω(k)
Acoustic modes start at zero frequency at k = 0
Optical modes can start at finite frequency
Determines sound, heat, and lattice response
Key in solid-state dynamics
860) Bloch oscillation
Electrons in periodic lattice under constant field can exhibit oscillatory motion in ideal models
Frequency proportional to field and lattice spacing
Quantum and band-structure effect
Observed in engineered systems
Important in mesoscopic and cold-atom physics
861) Tight-binding dispersion
E(k) = E0 - 2t cos(ka) in simplest 1D model
t is hopping amplitude
Bandwidth depends on coupling strength
Useful for electrons in lattices and chains
Captures band formation simply
862) Hopping model in 2D
Energy depends on lattice geometry and nearest-neighbor coupling
Used for square, triangular, and honeycomb lattices
Model of graphene-like systems
Band topology can emerge from hopping structure
Core condensed-matter approximation
863) Dirac-like dispersion
E(k) ≈ ±ħvF|k| near linear band touching
Common in graphene and other Dirac materials
Massless-fermion-like behavior emerges
Leads to unusual transport properties
Important modern condensed-matter formula
864) Landau level filling
Filling factor ν = nh/(eB)
Counts occupied magnetic levels in 2D electron systems
Central to quantum Hall effect
Depends on carrier density and field strength
Discrete quantum magnetotransport
865) Quantum Hall resistance
Rxy = h/(νe²)
Quantized plateaus observed experimentally
Extremely precise resistance standards
ν is integer or fractional in different regimes
Key quantum-transport result
866) Fractional quantum Hall idea
Interacting electrons can form correlated incompressible states
Fractional plateaus arise from many-body effects
Requires strong magnetic field and low temperature
Important in topological matter
Beyond single-particle physics
867) Topological invariant
Characterizes global band structure properties
Cannot change without closing the gap
Explains robust edge states in topological phases
Used in modern condensed matter theory
Not a local order parameter
868) Chern number
Integer topological index from Berry curvature integration over Brillouin zone
Quantizes Hall response in topological bands
Central in quantum Hall physics
Protected under smooth perturbations
Important topological quantity
869) Berry curvature
Acts like magnetic field in momentum space
Influences anomalous velocity and transport
Integral gives topological invariants
Useful in band theory and semiclassics
Core object in modern materials theory
870) Kubo formula
Linear response conductivity from current-current correlation
Connects microscopic dynamics to macroscopic transport
Used in quantum and statistical mechanics
Foundation of conductivity calculations
Powerful but formal expression
871) Drude conductivity
σ = ne²τ/m
τ is relaxation time
Simple model of metallic conduction
Gives Ohm’s law microscopically
Foundation of classical transport theory
872) Mobility relation
μ = eτ/m
Drift velocity = μE
Mobility measures ease of carrier motion
Depends on scattering and band structure
Important in semiconductors
873) Wiedemann-Franz law
κ/(σT) ≈ constant for many metals
Links heat and charge transport
Approximate Lorenz number relation
Valid in degenerate electron regime
Important for metals and transport theory
874) Seebeck coefficient
S = -ΔV/ΔT under open-circuit thermal bias in simple definition
Measures thermoelectric voltage response
Can be positive or negative depending on carrier type
Important in power generation and sensing
Thermoelectric transport quantity
875) Hall mobility
μH = |RH|σ
Combines Hall coefficient and conductivity
Experimental measure of carrier motion
Useful in semiconductor characterization
Relates to scattering and density
876) Mean free path
ℓ = vτ
Distance traveled between scattering events
Connects microscopic time and length scales
Important in gases, electrons, and phonons
Used in transport regimes
877) Knudsen number
Kn = ℓ/L
Measures rarefaction relative to system size
Kn << 1 continuum regime
Kn >> 1 free-molecular regime
Important in microfluidics and vacuum physics
878) Plasma beta
β = gas pressure / magnetic pressure
Compares thermal to magnetic dominance
β << 1 magnetically dominated plasma
β >> 1 gas pressure dominates
Key in astrophysical plasma dynamics
879) Alfven speed
vA = B/√(μ0ρ)
Magnetic tension sets wave speed
Important in plasmas and space physics
Determines propagation of Alfvén waves
Central MHD quantity
880) Alfvén wave
Transverse wave propagating along magnetic field lines in magnetized plasma
Restoring force is magnetic tension
Used in space plasma and solar physics
Distinct from sound waves
Fundamental MHD wave mode
881) Magnetosonic speed
Combines sound and Alfvénic effects in plasma waves
Fast and slow modes exist in MHD
Depends on field angle and plasma beta
Used in astrophysical plasma modeling
Wave speed from coupled restoring forces
882) Debye shielding length revisited
Potential perturbations decay over characteristic screening distance
Charged particles rearrange to reduce electric field
Higher temperature weakens shielding
Higher density strengthens shielding
Important in electrolytes and plasmas
883) Euler-Maclaurin idea
Relates sums to integrals with correction terms
Useful for approximating series and asymptotics
Appears in statistical mechanics and numerics
Connects discrete and continuous descriptions
Advanced mathematical tool
884) Saddle-point approximation
Integral dominated by neighborhoods near stationary points
Useful for large-parameter asymptotics
Common in statistical mechanics and quantum path integrals
Approximates difficult integrals efficiently
Important in advanced physics
885) Path integral weight
Amplitude ∝ e^(iS/ħ)
Classical path contributes by stationary action
Quantum evolution summed over all paths
Central formulation in quantum mechanics and field theory
Alternative to operator approach
886) Euclidean action
Used after Wick rotation t → -iτ
Weight becomes e^(-SE/ħ) in many contexts
Useful for statistical mechanics and tunneling
Improves convergence of integrals
Widely used in field theory
887) Wick rotation
Transforms oscillatory integrals into decaying exponentials
t to imaginary time simplifies some problems
Connects quantum mechanics and thermal theory
Mathematical technique rather than physical motion
Important in theoretical physics
888) Partition function from path integral
Z = ∫ D[x] e^(-SE/ħ) in Euclidean form
Encodes thermodynamic and quantum information
Used for lattice and field calculations
Powerful but formal framework
Connects microstates to observables
889) Correlation function
C(r) =
Measures spatial or temporal dependence of fluctuations
Decay length reveals characteristic scale
Important in critical phenomena and materials
Links theory to experiment
890) Critical scaling
Near critical point, observables often follow power laws
Exponent values characterize universality class
Correlation length diverges in ideal theory
Used in phase transitions and statistical physics
Scale invariance emerges
891) Renormalization idea
Effective description changes with scale
Coupling constants may flow under coarse graining
Explains universality and critical exponents
Used in condensed matter and field theory
One of the most important modern concepts
892) Euler characteristic in topology
χ = V - E + F for polyhedral surfaces
Generalizes to more complex topological spaces
Connects geometry and topology
Useful in classification problems
Appears in physics with topological defects
893) Topological defect charge
Defect classification can involve winding numbers or homotopy invariants
Examples include vortices, domain walls, and monopole-like textures
Stable because of topology rather than energy alone
Important in condensed matter and cosmology
Not removable by smooth deformation
894) Winding number
Counts how many times a phase wraps around a cycle
Integral of gradient around closed loop yields 2πn in ideal case
Important in vortices and superconductors
Topological integer quantity
Used in many branches of physics
895) Vortex circulation
Γ = ∮ v · dl
Quantized in superfluids and superconductors in appropriate units
Measures rotation content of flow
Important in fluid dynamics and quantum fluids
Connects to vorticity
896) Vorticity theorem
For inviscid barotropic flow, vorticity evolves with stretching and tilting terms
Useful in fluid and atmospheric dynamics
Helps explain vortex amplification
Important in turbulence and geophysical flows
Mathematical form more complex than scalar rotation
897) Kelvin circulation theorem
Circulation conserved in ideal barotropic flow with conservative body forces
Classical fluid analog of conserved quantities from symmetry
Useful for vortex motion analysis
Applies under specific ideal assumptions
Important in fluid mechanics
898) Helmholtz decomposition
Vector field can be written as gradient part plus curl part under suitable conditions
Useful in electromagnetism and fluid mechanics
Separates irrotational and solenoidal components
Mathematical tool for field analysis
Very widely used
899) Hodge-style decomposition
Generalization of vector decomposition on manifolds
Separates exact, coexact, and harmonic parts
Important in differential geometry and field theory
Used in advanced mathematical physics
Beyond elementary vector calculus

901) Differential forms
ω = Σ aI dx^I
d² = 0
Closed form: dω = 0
Exact form: ω = dη
Wedge product: dx^i ∧ dx^j = -dx^j ∧ dx^i
902) Exterior derivative
d(fg) = f dg + g df
d(α ∧ β) = dα ∧ β + (-1)^p α ∧ dβ for p-form α
Generalizes grad, curl, and div
Built to preserve orientation structure
Central in modern geometry
903) Hodge star
* maps p-forms to (n-p)-forms
**² sign depends on dimension and metric convention
Used to define dual fields
Important in electromagnetism and geometry
Pairs differential forms with volume elements
904) Electromagnetic forms
F = dA
dF = 0
d*F = J
A is the 4-potential
Compact form of Maxwell theory
905) Gauge field action
S = -1/4 ∫ FμνFμν d⁴x
Gauge invariance under Aμ → Aμ + ∂μχ
Field equations follow from variation
Foundation of classical and quantum electrodynamics
Forms basis of nonabelian generalization
906) Klein-Gordon equation
(□ + m²c²/ħ²)φ = 0
Relativistic scalar field equation
□ = ∂μ∂μ in covariant notation
Describes spin-0 particles
Key wave equation in relativistic quantum theory
907) Dirac equation
(iħγμ∂μ - mc)ψ = 0
Relativistic spin-1/2 wave equation
Predicts antimatter and spin naturally
γμ satisfy Clifford algebra
Foundational equation of fermion physics
908) Gamma matrices
{γμ, γν} = 2ημνI
Clifford algebra relation
Used in Dirac theory and relativistic spinors
Matrix structure encodes spacetime signature
Important in high-energy physics
909) Feynman propagator
G_F(x - y) = ⟨0|Tφ(x)φ(y)|0⟩
Describes amplitude propagation between spacetime points
Time ordering appears explicitly
Used in perturbative quantum field theory
Central Green-function object
910) Scattering amplitude
Mfi determines transition probability
dσ ∝ |Mfi|² × phase space
Cross section relates amplitude to measurable rate
Computed using perturbation expansion in interactions
Core object in particle physics
911) Phase-space element
dΓ = Πi d³pi/(2Ei(2π)³)
Represents available final-state states
Used in decay rates and cross sections
Important for kinematic integration
Relativistically invariant measure
912) Decay rate
Γ = 1/τ
N(t) = N0 e^-Γt
Lifetime and width linked by uncertainty relation
Exponential decay is common in unstable systems
Used in nuclear and particle physics
913) Bremsstrahlung intuition
Accelerated charges radiate
Radiated power increases with acceleration strength
Important in deceleration of electrons near nuclei
Generates continuous X-ray spectra
Radiation loss mechanism in accelerators
914) Synchrotron spectrum
Radiation from relativistic charge in curved trajectory
Emission concentrated in forward cone
Spectrum broad and intense
Strongly depends on energy and curvature radius
Important in storage rings and astrophysics
915) Cherenkov condition
v > c/n
Light emitted when particle moves faster than phase velocity in medium
Emission angle satisfies cos θ = c/(nv)
Produces characteristic blue glow
Used in detectors and neutrino observatories
916) Plasma dispersion
ω² = ωp² + c²k² for simple electromagnetic waves in plasma
Low-frequency cutoff appears below plasma frequency
Medium response depends on charge density
Important in ionized media
Core plasma-wave relation
917) Debye-Hückel potential
V(r) ∝ e^-r/λD / r
Screened Coulomb potential in electrolyte or plasma
λD is screening length
Long-range electric interactions are reduced
Useful in soft matter and plasma theory
918) Langevin magnetism
M = NμL(μB/kT)
Langevin function describes paramagnetic alignment
Approaches linear response at weak fields
Approaches saturation at strong fields
Used in classical paramagnetism
919) Curie law
χ = C/T
Magnetic susceptibility decreases with temperature in paramagnets
Simple high-temperature approximation
Useful in magnetism and materials science
Shows thermal disordering of moments
920) Curie-Weiss law
χ = C/(T - θ)
θ indicates interaction tendency
Can signal ferromagnetic or antiferromagnetic behavior
Improves over simple Curie law
Widely used in magnetic characterization
921) Exchange interaction
Heisenberg model: H = -J Σ Si · Sj
J > 0 favors ferromagnetism in common sign convention
J < 0 favors antiferromagnetism
Quantum spin coupling produces collective order
Foundational magnetism model
922) Ising model
H = -J Σ si sj - h Σ si
si = ±1 spin variables
Displays phase transition in low dimensions and finite dimensions depending on temperature
Canonical model of statistical mechanics
Explains order-disorder phenomena
923) Partition function for Ising systems
Z = Σ exp(-βH)
All thermodynamic quantities derive from Z
Exact in 1D and special cases, numerical otherwise
Central in lattice statistical mechanics
Describes collective spin behavior
924) Boltzmann factor
P ∝ e^-E/kT
Lower energy states are more probable at equilibrium
Foundation of canonical ensemble
Appears throughout statistical physics
Connects energy and probability
925) Entropy from microstates
S = kB ln Ω
Ω counts accessible microstates
More microstates means higher entropy
Statistical basis of thermodynamics
Extremely important conceptual relation
926) Free energy in statistical mechanics
F = -kBT ln Z
Helmholtz free energy comes from partition function
Minimized at fixed T and V in equilibrium
Connects microscopic states to macroscopic work potential
Key quantity in ensemble theory
927) Grand canonical ensemble
Ξ = Σ exp[-β(E - μN)]
Used when particle number fluctuates
Grand potential Ω = -kBT ln Ξ
Common in quantum gases and open systems
Very useful for variable-particle problems
928) Chemical potential
μ = (∂G/∂N)T,P
Controls particle exchange equilibrium
Equality of μ across phases or systems gives balance
Important in thermodynamics and diffusion
Central in statistical mechanics
929) Landau free energy
F = F0 + aη² + bη⁴ + ...
Order parameter η describes phase transition
Coefficient signs determine stability and broken symmetry
Useful in critical phenomena and ferroelectrics
Phenomenological phase-transition model
930) Order parameter
Quantifies degree of symmetry breaking
Zero in disordered phase, nonzero in ordered phase in many systems
Examples: magnetization, density difference, superconducting gap
Important in phase-transition theory
Not always unique
931) Mean-field approximation
Replace interactions by average field
Reduces many-body problem to simpler effective single-body description
Often captures qualitative transitions
Can miss fluctuations in low dimensions
Widely used in condensed matter
932) Critical exponent scaling
Correlation length: ξ ∼ |T - Tc|^-ν
Susceptibility: χ ∼ |T - Tc|^-γ
Order parameter: η ∼ (Tc - T)^β for T < Tc
Heat capacity: C ∼ |T - Tc|^-α
Universality classes share the same critical exponents despite different microscopic details
933) Correlation length
ξ measures size of correlated regions
Diverges near continuous phase transitions in ideal theory
Large ξ means long-range fluctuations
Appears in critical phenomena and statistical fields
Determines scaling behavior
934) Renormalization group flow
dgi/dln b = βi(g)
Couplings evolve with scale
Fixed points control universal behavior
Relevant, irrelevant, and marginal operators classify perturbations
Central in modern theoretical physics
935) Kramers-Kronig relation
Real and imaginary parts of response functions are linked by causality
Dispersion and absorption are not independent
Used in optics, dielectric response, and spectroscopy
Mathematical consequence of analytic continuation
Very important in linear response
936) Susceptibility
M = χH
P = ε0χe E
Response proportionality in linear regime
Complex susceptibility includes loss and phase lag
Foundation of material response theory
937) Complex permittivity
ε(ω) = ε' - iε''
Real part stores energy
Imaginary part dissipates energy
Frequency dependence encodes dispersion and loss

938) Complex permeability
μ(ω) = μ' - iμ''
Describes frequency-dependent magnetic response
Losses appear in imaginary component
Important in magnetic materials and metamaterials
Generalizes static magnetic permeability
939) Skin effect in conductors
Current density concentrates near surface at high frequency
Penetration depth shrinks as frequency rises
Reduces effective conducting area

940) Ohmic heating
P = I²R
Power dissipation in resistors and conductors
Causes temperature rise

941) Joule-Thomson effect
Temperature change in throttling process under constant enthalpy
Sign depends on inversion temperature
Used in gas liquefaction and refrigeration
Real-gas effect absent in ideal gas
Important thermodynamic phenomenon
942) Inversion temperature
Joule-Thomson coefficient changes sign at inversion curve
Above inversion temperature, expansion may warm the gas
Below it, expansion may cool the gas
Relevant in cryogenics and gas processing
Depends on intermolecular forces
943) Adiabatic index
γ = Cp/Cv
Controls speed of sound and adiabatic relations
Monatomic ideal gas: γ = 5/3
Diatomic gas: approximately 7/5 at ordinary temperatures
Important in gas dynamics
944) Speed of sound in ideal gas
v = √(γRT/M)
Depends on temperature and molecular mass
Higher temperature gives faster sound
Lower molar mass gives faster sound
Useful in acoustics and gas dynamics
945) Shock Hugoniot relation
Links pre-shock and post-shock states via conservation laws
Applies across discontinuities in compressible flow
Important in supersonic aerodynamics
Pressure, density, and velocity jump across shock
Advanced fluid mechanics relation
946) Rarefaction wave
Expansion fan in compressible flow
Pressure and density decrease smoothly rather than jump
Occurs in high-speed gas dynamics
Complementary to shock waves
Important in transient compressible flow
947) Rayleigh criterion for stability
Rotation stable if specific angular momentum increases outward in ideal fluid context
Used in rotating flows and astrophysical disks
Helps diagnose shear instabilities
Important in fluid stability theory
Applies in special conditions
948) Kelvin-Helmholtz instability
Occurs when shear between layers overcomes stabilizing forces
Produces rolling waves at interfaces
Important in clouds, oceans, and astrophysics
Driven by velocity difference across boundary
Classic fluid instability
949) Rayleigh-Taylor instability
Heavy fluid above light fluid under gravity can be unstable
Small perturbations grow into fingers or plumes
Important in inertial confinement and astrophysics
Triggered when density stratification is inverted
Fundamental instability mechanism
950) Faraday instability
Periodic forcing can destabilize fluid surface
Produces standing wave patterns
Parametric resonance in fluids
Important in vibrating containers and pattern formation
Links to nonlinear dynamics
951) Capillary number
Ca = μv/γ
Compares viscous to surface-tension forces
Low Ca means surface tension dominates
High Ca means viscous effects dominate
Important in droplets and microfluidics
952) Weber number
We = ρv²L/γ
Compares inertial to surface-tension forces
High We favors breakup and deformation

953) Froude number
Fr = v/√(gL)
Compares inertial to gravitational effects

954) Mach number
Ma = v/c
Compares flow speed to sound speed
Subsonic, transonic, supersonic, and hypersonic regimes

955) Prandtl number
Pr = ν/α
Compares momentum diffusivity to thermal diffusivity

956) Nusselt number
Nu = hL/k

957) Rayleigh number
Ra = gβΔTL³/(να)
Controls onset of convection in heated fluids

Central in thermal instability analysis
958) Biot number
Bi = hL/k

959) Lumped capacitance model
dT/dt ∝ -(T - T∞)
Valid when Bi is small
Temperature uniform inside object
Exponential cooling or heating behavior
Used in thermal transients
960) Newton’s law of cooling
dT/dt = -k(T - Tenv)
Temperature difference drives heat loss rate in simple model
Solution is exponential approach to ambient temperature
Approximate but useful

961) Stefan problem
Moving phase boundary determined by heat diffusion and latent heat balance
Used in melting and freezing front dynamics
Requires coupling temperature field and boundary motion
Important in phase-change materials
Advanced heat-transfer problem
962) Diffusion-limited growth
Growth rate controlled by transport of material to interface
Common in crystallization and deposition
Leads to branching patterns in some regimes
Important in materials and pattern formation
Transport constraints dominate kinetics
963) Nernst diffusion layer
Thin layer near electrode controls concentration gradient
Current can become diffusion-limited
Important in electrochemistry and mass transfer
Concentration polarization develops
Used in batteries and corrosion
964) Butler-Volmer equation
Current overpotential relation for electrochemical kinetics
I = I0[exp(αaFη/RT) - exp(-αcFη/RT)]
Describes charge-transfer reactions
Important in batteries, fuel cells, and electrodes
Combines forward and reverse reaction rates
965) Tafel approximation
At large overpotential, one exponential dominates Butler-Volmer form
Log current varies linearly with overpotential
Used to analyze electrode kinetics
Important in electrochemistry
Practical simplification of nonlinear relation
966) Diffusion potential
Potential difference created by concentration gradient of ions
Arises in electrolytes and semipermeable systems
Important in cells and biological membranes
Driven by unequal ion mobilities
Electrochemical transport effect
967) Nernst equation for concentration cell
E = E° - (RT/nF)ln Q
Voltage depends on reaction quotient
Applies in electrochemistry and membranes
Core relation for electrochemical potentials
Standard and nonstandard conditions differ
968) Membrane potential
Potential across biological or synthetic membrane depends on ion gradients and selectivity
Often modeled by Nernst or Goldman type relations
Important in electrophysiology
Relevant to cells and ion transport
Electrochemical balance concept
969) Goldman-Hodgkin-Katz idea
Membrane voltage depends on multiple ion permeabilities and concentrations
Extends simple Nernst equilibrium
970) Electrostatic boundary condition
E⊥,out - E⊥,in = σ/ε0
E∥ continuous in electrostatics
Potential continuous across interface
Applied to conductors and dielectrics
Foundation for interface problems
971) Displacement current
Jd = ε0 ∂E/∂t
Completes Ampère’s law
Allows consistency with charge conservation
Essential for changing electric fields
Key part of Maxwell equations
972) Maxwell-Ampère law
∮ B · dl = μ0(I + ε0 dΦE/dt)
Magnetic field generated by conduction current and changing electric flux
Crucial for electromagnetic waves
Generalizes magnetostatics
One of Maxwell’s equations
973) Electromagnetic wave equation
□E = 0 and □B = 0 in vacuum
Wave speed c arises from ε0 and μ0
Fields are mutually supporting in propagation
Foundation of light as EM wave
Central wave equation
974) Poynting vector
S = (1/μ0)E × B
Represents EM energy flux
Direction gives power flow direction
Magnitude gives transported power per area
Important in radiation and circuits
975) Radiation impedance
Antennas and radiating structures convert current to outgoing waves
Real part of impedance corresponds to radiated power
Reactive part stores near-field energy
Key in antenna efficiency
Used in RF design
976) Skin depth in plasma
Field penetration depends on plasma frequency and collision rate
Low-frequency cutoff and attenuation both occur
Important in ionized media
Extends conductor skin effect concepts
Used in space and fusion physics
977) Debye length in semiconductors
λD = √(εkBT/q²n)
Charge screening length in carrier systems
Sets electrostatic scale in devices
Important in junctions and plasmas
Analogous to electrolyte screening
978) Poisson-Boltzmann equation
∇²φ = -ρ/ε coupled with Boltzmann ion distribution in simple electrostatic systems
Nonlinear screening equation
Used in colloids, electrolytes, and biophysics
Combines electrostatics and statistical mechanics
Advanced electrochemical model
979) Helmholtz free energy in fields
F = U - TS
Useful at fixed temperature and volume
Equilibrium minimizes F
Applies in magnetism, elasticity, and mixtures
General thermodynamic potential
980) Grand potential
Ω = U - TS - μN
Natural for systems with particle exchange
Minimized in grand canonical ensemble
Important in quantum gases and open systems
Central in statistical mechanics
981) Specific heat anomaly
Nonanalytic behavior near phase transitions
Can diverge or show cusp-like peak
Signals critical behavior
Important in experiments on materials
Associated with fluctuations
982) Latent heat per particle
L/N reflects energy absorbed or released in phase transition
Connected to entropy difference via L = TΔS
Important in equilibrium thermodynamics
Used to analyze first-order transitions
Per-particle form useful in microscopic interpretation
983) Clapeyron slope
dP/dT = L/(TΔv)
Coexistence line slope depends on latent heat and volume change
Very useful in phase diagrams
Applies to melting and vaporization lines
Fundamental thermodynamic relation
984) Maxwell construction
Equal-area rule removes unphysical oscillation in van der Waals isotherm
Determines phase coexistence pressure
Used in first-order phase transition analysis
Equivalent to equality of chemical potentials
Classical thermodynamic construction
985) Critical opalescence
Scattering grows strongly near critical point due to large fluctuations
Medium becomes visually cloudy
Evidence of diverging correlation length
Observed near liquid-gas criticality
Important in phase-transition experiments
986) Percolation threshold
Connectivity appears above critical occupation probability
Cluster formation becomes system-spanning
Relevant in porous media, networks, and transport
Phase-transition-like behavior in disordered systems
Important statistical concept
987) Random walk
Mean squared displacement grows proportional to number of steps
In continuum limit, leads to diffusion
Foundation of stochastic transport models
Used in physics and finance
Simple yet powerful process
988) Brownian diffusion constant
D = kBT/(6πηr) in Stokes-Einstein form for spherical particle
Relates diffusion to viscous drag
Higher temperature increases diffusion
Larger particles diffuse more slowly
Important in soft matter
989) Stokes drag
F = 6πηrv
Low-Reynolds-number drag on sphere
Linear in speed in creeping flow
Used in particle transport and sedimentation
Basis of terminal velocity models
990) Terminal settling speed
Balance weight, buoyancy, and drag
Settling speed determined when net force is zero
Depends on size, density difference, and viscosity
Used in suspensions and aerosols
Important in fluid mechanics
991) Sedimentation length
Characteristic scale for particles in gravitational field against thermal motion
Combines potential energy and entropy effects
Useful in colloids and soft matter
Controls concentration profile
Advanced statistical mechanics concept
992) Ornstein-Uhlenbeck process
dx = -γx dt + σ dW
Mean-reverting stochastic process
Gaussian stationary distribution in simple form
Used in noise and thermal fluctuation models
Continuous-time random dynamics
993) Power spectral density
S(ω) describes frequency content of fluctuations
Integral over frequency gives variance in many contexts
Used in noise analysis and signal processing
Important in experiment and theory
Connects time-domain and frequency-domain behavior
994) Allan variance
Measures frequency stability over averaging time
Used in clocks, oscillators, and precision metrology
Sensitive to drift and noise type
Useful for time-series characterization
Advanced stability metric
995) Coherence function
g(1)(τ) measures phase correlation between field values
g(2)(τ) measures intensity correlations
Important in quantum optics and lasers
Characterizes statistical light properties
Useful for photon counting and interference
996) Photon antibunching
g(2)(0) < 1 indicates nonclassical light
Single-photon emission signature
Important in quantum optics
Reveals discrete nature of light
Used in quantum communication
997) Stimulated emission
Photon triggers emission of identical photon from excited state
Basis of laser operation
Requires population inversion
Amplifies coherent radiation
Key quantum optical process
998) Population inversion
Upper state more populated than lower state in relevant transition
Necessary for optical gain
Requires pumping and non-equilibrium
Core laser prerequisite
Important in photonics
999) Laser threshold
Gain equals losses at threshold
Above threshold, oscillation can sustain itself
Depends on cavity, medium, and pump rate
Determines onset of laser action
Central design condition
1000) Mode competition
Multiple cavity modes compete for gain
Nonlinear saturation selects dominant modes
Determines laser spectrum and stability
Important in resonators and lasers
Advanced photonics concept

Table 5
Physics Formula Bank
1001) Saturable absorption
Absorber transmission increases with intensity above a threshold-like regime
Used for passive mode locking
Nonlinear optical effect
Important in lasers and pulse generation
Controls temporal behavior
1002) Mode locking
Phase locking of longitudinal modes produces short pulses

Enables ultrafast laser output

1003) Pulse duration-bandwidth relation
Shorter pulse implies broader spectrum
Time-frequency uncertainty appears in signal form

1004) Gaussian pulse
E(t) ∝ exp(-t²/2τ²) cos(ω0 t)
Spectrum also Gaussian in ideal case
Used as a standard model for ultrashort pulses
Mathematically convenient and physically common

1005) Frequency comb
Discrete equally spaced optical lines
Line spacing set by pulse repetition rate
Extremely precise metrology tool
Used in spectroscopy and frequency standards

1006) Atomic clock stability
Clock transition frequency serves as reference
Fractional instability improves with averaging time

1007) Hyperfine transition
Energy splitting from nuclear-electron magnetic interaction
Important in atomic clocks

Used in spectroscopy and quantum standards

1008) Rydberg atom
Highly excited atom with large principal quantum number
Radius scales as n²
Polarizability and dipole moment can be huge
Strongly interacting and long-lived

1009) Polarizability
p = αE
Induced dipole moment proportional to field in linear regime

Important in atoms and molecules

1010) van der Waals interaction
Long-range intermolecular force often scales as -C6/r⁶ in leading form
Arises from induced dipoles and fluctuations
Important in condensed matter and chemistry
Weak but ubiquitous interaction
Not the same as hard-sphere repulsion
1011) Lennard-Jones potential
U(r) = 4ε[(σ/r)^12 - (σ/r)^6]
Repulsive short range, attractive long range
Widely used model for neutral atoms and molecules
Parameters set depth and equilibrium distance
Common in simulation
1012) Molecular dynamics force
F = -∇U
Atoms evolve under potential gradients
Numerical time integration approximates trajectories
Used in chemistry and materials simulation
Many-body computational method
1013) Verlet integration
r(t + Δt) = 2r(t) - r(t - Δt) + a(t)Δt²
Simple symplectic-like numerical integrator
Good for molecular dynamics
Conserves energy better than some naive schemes
Widely used in simulation
1014) Runge-Kutta idea
Higher-order finite-step ODE solver
Combines intermediate slope estimates
Improves accuracy over Euler method
Used broadly in numerical physics
Standard computational tool
1015) Stability of numerical schemes
Time step must respect stability constraints
Too large a step can cause divergence
CFL condition is common in wave and fluid solvers
Important in numerical PDEs
Essential computational consideration
1016) Courant condition
Δt ≤ Δx/v in many explicit wave schemes
Ensures signal does not outrun grid stability
Important in finite-difference methods
Depends on discretization and wave speed
Core numerical stability criterion
1017) Finite-difference Laplacian
∇²f approximated by neighboring grid values

Accuracy depends on grid spacing
Fundamental numerical PDE tool
Computational physics staple
1018) Monte Carlo error
Statistical error decreases as 1/√N
Random sampling estimates integrals and averages

1019) Importance sampling
Sample more frequently where contribution is large
Reduces variance compared with naive random sampling
Used in Monte Carlo simulation
Improves efficiency substantially
Important computational method
1020) Metropolis algorithm
Accept moves with probability min(1, e^-βΔE)
Samples equilibrium distributions

Classic simulation method
1021) Markov chain
Next state depends only on current state
Transition matrix determines evolution

1022) Detailed balance
πi Pij = πj Pji
Ensures equilibrium distribution in many stochastic systems

1023) Ergodicity
Time averages equal ensemble averages in the long run under suitable conditions

Allows one trajectory to represent the ensemble

1024) Ensemble average
⟨A⟩ = Σ Ai pi or integral over state space

1025) Fluctuation relation

1026) Equipartition theorem

1027) Maxwell-Boltzmann speed moments

1028) Molecular collision frequency

1112) Width-lifetime relation
Γ ≈ ħ/τ

1128) Einstein relation

1135) Entropy production

1201) Linear algebra of state evolution
x_{n+1} = A x_n
Repeated application of A determines long-term behavior
Eigenvalues control growth, decay, and oscillation
Diagonalization simplifies many iterative systems
Used in discrete dynamics and numerical schemes
1202) Discrete-time oscillation
x_n = A cos(nθ + φ)
Equivalent to rotation on a phase circle in ideal lossless case
Frequency in steps determined by θ
Useful for sampled signals and maps
Discrete analogue of SHM
1203) Difference equations
x_{n+1} - x_n = f(n, x_n)
Finite-step version of differential equations
Used in numerical time stepping and population models
Stability depends on step size and coefficients
Important in computational physics
1204) Logistic map
x_{n+1} = r x_n(1 - x_n)
Shows fixed points, period doubling, and chaos
Simple nonlinear discrete model
Used to illustrate nonlinear dynamics
Sensitive dependence on parameter r
1205) Fixed-point iteration
x_{n+1} = g(x_n)
Converges when |g'(x*)| < 1 near fixed point
Common root-finding method
Can fail if iteration is unstable
Useful in numerical analysis
1206) Newton-Raphson method
x_{n+1} = x_n - f(x_n)/f'(x_n)
Quadratic convergence near root when conditions are met
Used to solve equations numerically
Requires derivative information
Powerful root-finding tool
1207) Secant method
x_{n+1} = x_n - f(x_n)(x_n - x_{n-1})/[f(x_n) - f(x_{n-1})]
Derivative-free root-finding method
Often converges faster than simple fixed-point iteration
Useful when derivatives are hard to compute
Widely used numerically
1208) Bisection method
If f(a)f(b) < 0, a root lies in [a,b]
Repeated interval halving guarantees convergence
Slow but robust
Used when reliability is more important than speed
Fundamental numerical method
1209) Trapezoidal rule
∫_a^b f(x)dx ≈ h[1/2 f(x_0) + f(x_1) + ... + 1/2 f(x_n)]
Approximates area by trapezoids
Accuracy improves as step size decreases
Useful in numerical integration
Basic quadrature formula
1210) Simpson’s rule
Approximates integral using parabolic segments
More accurate than trapezoidal rule for smooth functions
Requires even number of subintervals
Common in numerical analysis
Useful for data and simulation
1211) Monte Carlo integration
Integral estimated from random sampling average
Error often decreases as 1/√N
Useful in high-dimensional problems
Common in statistical physics and radiation transport
Powerful when deterministic quadrature is expensive
1212) Least-squares residual
r_i = y_i - f(x_i)
Residuals measure deviation of data from model
Minimizing Σr_i² gives best fit under Gaussian error assumptions
Used in regression and calibration
Core data-analysis concept
1213) Normal equations for linear fit
A^T A x = A^T b
Arises from least-squares minimization
Solution gives best-fit parameters in linear model
Useful in experimental data fitting

1214) Gram-Schmidt orthogonalization
Converts independent vectors into orthogonal basis
Useful in vector spaces and numerical linear algebra
Basis vectors become easier to work with
Important in quantum mechanics and mechanics
Foundational algebraic procedure
1215) Projection formula
proj_b(a) = (a·b/|b|²)b

Useful in mechanics, geometry, and optimization

1216) Cross-product geometry
|a × b| = |a||b|sinθ
Magnitude equals area of parallelogram formed by vectors
Direction perpendicular to both vectors
Used in torque and angular momentum

1217) Triple product
a·(b×c) = volume of parallelepiped

Useful in geometry and vector calculus

1218) Divergence theorem in physics
∭(∇·F)dV = ∬F·dA

1219) Stokes theorem in physics

1220) Laplacian in Cartesian coordinates

1221) Laplace equation

1223) Heat equation

1224) Wave equation

1225) Damped wave idea

1226) Diffusion length scale

1241) Reflection coefficient

1243) Power flow in waves

1247) Sampling theorem

1248) Aliasing

1249) Nyquist frequency

1251) Transfer function poles

1252) Transfer function zeros

1254) Bode magnitude

1255) Bode phase

1256) Nyquist stability idea

1257) Control-loop error

1258) PID control

Widely used in engineering systems

Standard feedback controller
1259) Phase margin
Measures how much additional phase lag a stable control loop can tolerate before instability
Important robustness metric
Used with gain margin
Common in control engineering
Stability indicator
1260) Gain margin
Measures how much loop gain can increase before instability
Important robustness metric in feedback design
Used with phase margin
Indicates stability reserve
Control-system criterion
1261) Mechanical quality factor
Q = 2π(energy stored)/(energy lost per cycle)
Higher Q means less damping and narrower resonance
Used in pendulums, resonators, and MEMS
Important for precision oscillators
Common oscillatory metric
1262) Damping ratio
ζ = c/(2√(km)) in standard second-order system
Determines underdamped, critically damped, or overdamped behavior
Used in mechanics and control
Important response parameter
Second-order dynamic classification
1263) Second-order step response
Rise, overshoot, and settling depend on ζ and ω_n
Used for control systems and mechanical systems
Describes response to sudden change
Important in engineering dynamics
Standard model behavior
1264) Natural frequency
ω_n = √(k/m) for mass-spring system
General notion applies to many systems
Characteristic undamped frequency
Used in vibration and resonance
Key system property
1265) Damped frequency
ω_d = ω_n√(1 - ζ²)
Applies in underdamped systems
Oscillates more slowly than undamped system
Used in vibration analysis
Relevant to transient response
1266) Logarithmic decrement
Measures damping from successive oscillation peaks
Used to estimate damping ratio experimentally
Helpful in structural vibration tests
Links amplitude decay to damping
Useful diagnostic quantity
1267) Structural resonance
Can amplify motion dramatically when excitation frequency matches natural modes
Important in buildings, bridges, and machinery
Must be avoided in design
Depends on damping and stiffness
Major engineering concern
1268) Modal analysis
System motion decomposed into normal modes
Each mode has its own frequency and shape
Used in mechanics, acoustics, and structures
Simplifies complex vibration problems
Standard analytical method
1269) Orthogonality of modes
Modes are orthogonal under appropriate inner product
Allows independent mode amplitudes
Crucial in series expansions and vibrations
Used in PDEs and structural dynamics

1270) Sturm-Liouville eigenvalue expansion
Solutions can be expanded in orthogonal eigenfunctions
Boundary conditions determine eigenvalues
Applies to many separated PDEs
Used in quantum and classical systems
Powerful eigenfunction framework
1271) Separation of variables
Assume solution is product of single-variable functions
Turns PDE into ODEs under appropriate geometry
Used in heat, wave, and Laplace equations
Boundary conditions determine allowed forms
Standard solution method
1272) Spherical coordinate Laplacian
∇² involves radial and angular parts with r and θ factors
Useful for central symmetry
Important in quantum and classical fields

1273) Cylindrical coordinate Laplacian

1274) Radial equation
Many central-force problems reduce to radial ODEs with effective potential

Essential in spherical symmetry problems

1275) Effective potential
U_eff(r) = U(r) + L²/(2mr²)

1276) Centrifugal barrier

1277) Turning point
Defined where kinetic energy in one coordinate vanishes

1278) WKB turning point matching

1279) Quantization condition

1280) Old quantum angular momentum

1283) Hydrogen ionization energy

1288) Relativistic invariant mass

1289) Four-momentum conservation

1290) Center-of-momentum frame

1291) Relativistic velocity addition

Accretion disk or orbital system quantities often depend on radius

Not a single universal formula, but radial dependence is central
Standard modeling variable
Astrophysical structure quantity
1409) Virial equilibrium in galaxies
2K + U ≈ 0 for bound system
Used to estimate galaxy and cluster masses
Relates velocity dispersion to gravitational binding
Important astrophysical tool
Approximate dynamical balance
1410) Jeans mass
Characteristic mass scale for gravitational collapse
Depends on temperature, density, and sound speed
Used in star formation theory
Determines stability of gas clouds
Collapse threshold quantity
1411) Jeans length
Characteristic instability wavelength for self-gravitating gas
Longer than this scale, collapse can occur
Important in astrophysical structure formation
Depends on sound speed and density

1412) Roche limit
Minimum distance before tidal disruption of satellite in simple density model
Depends on primary and secondary density
Important in planetary ring formation and breakup
Astrophysical tidal threshold
Classical disruption estimate
1413) Gravitational potential
Φ = -GM/r for point mass
Potential energy U = mΦ
Used in Newtonian gravity
Field g = -∇Φ
Analogous to electrostatic potential
1414) Poisson equation for gravity
∇²Φ = 4πGρ with sign convention depending on Φ definition
Newtonian gravity source equation
Used in astrophysics and geophysics
Classical field equation
Potential-source relation
1415) Gravitational field strength
g = GM/r²
Inverse-square gravitational acceleration magnitude
Used in planets and stars

1416) Weight
W = mg
Force due to gravity near Earth’s surface
Distinguish from mass
Vector quantity toward center of attracting body
Basic mechanics relation
1417) Terminal velocity with drag
At steady speed: weight = drag + buoyancy if present
Common in falling objects
Depends on drag law and object shape
Important in fluid mechanics and meteorology
Equilibrium-speed concept
1418) Reynolds number reminder
Re = ρvL/μ
Dimensionless criterion for flow regime
Low Re laminar, high Re often turbulent
Used in fluids and engineering
Key similarity parameter
1419) Continuum approximation
Material treated as continuous field rather than discrete particles
Valid when microscopic scales are much smaller than macroscopic variation scales
Used in fluids, solids, and electromagnetism

Modeling assumption
1420) Stress definition
σ = F/A
Force per unit area
Can be normal or shear depending on direction
Used in mechanics and materials
Core continuum quantity
1421) Strain definition
ε = ΔL/L0
Relative deformation
Used in elasticity and structural mechanics
Dimensionless quantity

1422) Hooke law in 1D
σ = Eε
E is Young’s modulus
Valid in linear elastic regime
Used in materials and structural analysis
Fundamental elasticity law
1423) Young modulus
E = stress/strain
Measures stiffness under tension or compression
Large E means stiff material
Important engineering property
Material response constant
1424) Shear modulus
G = shear stress / shear strain
Measures resistance to shape change
Important in solids and elasticity
Distinct from Young’s modulus

1425) Bulk modulus
K = -ΔP /(ΔV/V)
Measures resistance to compression
Used in fluids and solids

1426) Sound speed in solid rod
v = √(E/ρ) in simple rod approximation

1427) Thermal expansion stress
σth ≈ E α ΔT when expansion is constrained in simple model

1428) Fatigue failure
Repeated cyclic loading can lead to crack growth below static failure stress

1429) Yield criterion
Plastic deformation begins when stress state exceeds material-dependent threshold

1430) Mohr circle idea
Graphical representation of stress transformation in 2D
Useful for principal stresses and shear stress

1431) Principal stress
Normal stress on planes where shear stress vanishes
Found from eigenvalues of stress tensor
Important in structural analysis

1432) Principal strain
Strain tensor eigenvalues give principal strains
Used to analyze deformation without shear coupling
Important in elasticity and solid mechanics
Geometry of deformation

1433) Energy release rate
G measures energy available for crack growth per new crack area
Important in fracture mechanics
Crack growth occurs when G exceeds material toughness

1434) Stress intensity factor
K characterizes near-tip crack field

Important in engineering failure prediction

1435) Creep
Slow time-dependent deformation under constant stress
Important at high temperature or long times
Used in materials science and engineering

Deformation mechanism
1436) Viscous creep law
Strain rate often proportional to stress in Newtonian limit
Material-dependent viscosity appears
Used in fluids and viscoelastic solids
Time-dependent deformation relation

1437) Maxwell viscoelastic model
Spring and dashpot in series
Captures stress relaxation behavior
Used for viscoelastic materials

1438) Kelvin-Voigt model
Spring and dashpot in parallel
Captures creep behavior
Useful in viscoelastic solids

1439) Stress relaxation
Stress decreases over time under fixed strain in viscoelastic media

Models include exponential decay

1440) Creep compliance
Strain increases over time under constant stress
Useful in polymer mechanics and materials testing

1441) Phonon heat capacity low-T
C ∝ T³ in Debye model at low temperature for ordinary insulators

1442) Electronic heat capacity

1443) Wiedemann-Franz law
κ/(σT) ≈ constant

1445) Mobility edge

Series and parallel layers combine differently depending on current direction

1451) Lumped thermal capacitance
m c dT/dt = -hA(T - T∞)
Valid when Bi << 1
Temperature stays nearly uniform inside body
Used for cooling and heating transients
Simple first-order thermal model
1452) Heat transfer coefficient
Q̇ = hAΔT
Empirical convection relation in many settings
Higher h means stronger heat exchange
Depends on geometry and flow regime
Used in thermal design
1453) Thermal resistance network
Rth = ΔT/Q̇
Series thermal resistances add
Parallel paths combine reciprocally
Useful in conduction and convection analysis
Analogous to electric circuits
1454) Fin efficiency
ηf = actual heat transfer / ideal heat transfer
Measures performance of extended surfaces
Important in heat sinks and exchangers
Depends on fin shape and material

1455) Heat exchanger log-mean temperature difference
ΔTlm = (ΔT1 - ΔT2)/ln(ΔT1/ΔT2)
Used for counterflow and parallel-flow exchangers

1456) Exergy destruction
Exdest = T0 Sgen
Measures lost work potential due to irreversibility
Important in thermodynamic optimization

1457) Entropy generation
Sgen ≥ 0
Zero only for ideal reversible processes
Quantifies irreversibility
Central in nonequilibrium thermodynamics

1458) Second-law efficiency
ηII = actual performance / ideal reversible performance
Compares real device to thermodynamic limit
Useful for engines, refrigerators, and heat pumps

1459) Thermal diffusivity
α = k/(ρc)
Measures how quickly temperature spreads

1460) Fourier number
Fo = αt/L²

1461) Biot number
Bi = hL/k

1462) Prandtl number
Pr = ν/α

1463) Nusselt number
Nu = hL/k

1464) Reynolds number
Re = ρvL/μ

1465) Mach number
Ma = v/c

1466) Froude number

1467) Weber number

1468) Capillary number

1469) Grashof number

1471) Peclet number
Pe = vL/D for mass transport or Pe = vL/α for thermal transport

1472) Knudsen number
Kn = λmfp/L

1473) Strouhal number

1474) Rossby number
Ro = v/(2ΩL)

1476) Deborah number
De = relaxation time / observation time

1477) Weissenberg number
Wi = λγ̇

1478) Schmidt number
Sc = ν/D

1479) Lewis number
Le = α/D
Thermal diffusivity versus mass diffusivity
Important in coupled heat and mass transfer
Dimensionless transport measure

1480) Péclet heat balance
Advective transport dominates when Pe is large
Diffusion dominates when Pe is small
Useful in fluid and thermal systems
Helps choose modeling approximations
Transport regime indicator
1481) Viscosity-temperature relation
η often decreases with temperature in liquids and increases in gases under simple models
Material-specific empirical behavior
Important in fluid flow and lubrication
Strongly affects Reynolds number
Transport property trend
1482) Arrhenius law
Rate = A e^(-Ea/kT)
Thermally activated processes become faster at higher temperature
Used in diffusion, reactions, and materials
Central activation-energy formula
Temperature dependence law
1483) Activation energy
Ea is barrier that controls rate sensitivity to temperature
Extracted from Arrhenius plots
Important in chemistry, diffusion, and conduction
Higher Ea means stronger temperature dependence
Energy barrier concept
1484) Arrhenius plot
ln(rate) versus 1/T gives straight line in simple activated model
Slope yields activation energy
Useful for experimental analysis
Common in kinetics and transport
Data linearization tool
1485) Transition state intuition
Reaction rate controlled by highest free-energy bottleneck along path
Useful in chemical kinetics and materials processes
Activation barrier determines exponential suppression
Often modeled with rate theory
Barrier-crossing picture
1486) Rate equation
dx/dt = f(x)
Dynamics determined by growth and loss terms
Used in kinetics and population models
Steady state satisfies f(x)=0
General evolution equation
1487) Population balance
dN/dt = birth - death
Simple model for decay and growth processes
Used in nuclear, chemical, and biological systems
Exponential decay is special case
Rate-based modeling tool
1488) Exponential relaxation
x(t) = x0 e^(-t/τ)
Generic first-order decay toward equilibrium
τ is relaxation time
Used in circuits, thermal systems, and kinetics
Universal transient form
1489) Logarithmic decay
Some systems relax non-exponentially with broad time scales
Used in complex media and disordered systems
Appears in aging and anomalous kinetics
Not a single universal formula
Useful qualitative category
1490) Power-law decay
x(t) ∝ t^-n
Occurs in scale-free or critical systems
Slower than exponential decay
Important in turbulence and criticality
Common asymptotic behavior
1491) Fractional diffusion
Generalized transport can involve noninteger derivatives
Models anomalous diffusion and memory effects
Used in complex media
Captures heavy-tailed waiting times
Advanced transport model
1492) Langevin force balance
m dv/dt = -γv + ξ(t)
Random forcing plus viscous damping
Describes Brownian particles
Basis of stochastic dynamics
Classic noisy equation
1493) White noise
⟨ξ(t)ξ(t')⟩ ∝ δ(t - t')
Idealized uncorrelated random forcing
Used in stochastic differential equations
Mathematical noise model
Important in random processes
1494) Ornstein-Uhlenbeck process
dx = -λx dt + σ dW
Mean-reverting stochastic process
Common model for noisy relaxation
Used in thermal and financial analogies
Gaussian stationary process
1495) Fokker-Planck equation
∂P/∂t = -∂(aP)/∂x + 1/2 ∂²(bP)/∂x²
Evolution of probability density for stochastic systems
Describes drift and diffusion together
Used in statistical physics
Probability transport equation
1496) Master equation
dP_i/dt = Σ_j [W_{ji}P_j - W_{ij}P_i]
Transition-rate equation for discrete states
Used in kinetics and Markov processes
Models birth-death and jump dynamics
General probabilistic evolution
1497) Detailed balance in Markov systems
π_i W_{ij} = π_j W_{ji}
Equilibrium condition for reversible stochastic dynamics
Important in Monte Carlo and kinetics
Guarantees stationary distribution
Probability-flow symmetry
1498) Metastable lifetime
τ often grows exponentially with barrier height in simple activated systems
Important in nucleation and switching
Rare-event timescale concept
Used in materials and chemistry

1499) Kramers rate
Escape rate over barrier depends on damping, barrier height, and temperature
Important in chemical reaction dynamics and noise-driven switching

Used in stochastic systems
Barrier-crossing rate law
1500) Thermally activated switching
Probability of switching grows with temperature and field
Relevant in magnets, memristors, and devices

1586) Finite-difference time stepping
